93
==PAGE:101==
Chapter 6
Conclusion
The overall objective of this project was to validate and assess FBIM simulations in a Danish
context. To that end, four experiments containing key firefighting activities have been success-
fully employed to serve as a baseline for Danish intervention processes. To do this, a common
ground or paradigm has been established and related to the use of FBIM in a Danish setting.
From this understanding and the FBIM methodologies in [2][35][36], the individual FBIM data
were reviewed and assessed. This was done to examine the source of FBIM and the dataset it
relies on and to identify the scope of the experiments.
As such, 27 firefighting activities were determined to be included in the investigations of this
project. These were intended to either validate corresponding FBIM data or to implement
and outline activities that are not represented in FBIM, all of which are considered commonly
deployed by Danish fire and rescue services.
To validate and assess the overall methodology of FBIM, a fire scenario was deemed necessary to
include in this project. The fire scenario was intended for direct comparison with corresponding
and equivalent FBIM simulations. Therefore, the fire scenario was devised to represent a basic
and general case of a Danish intervention process. The aim was to illuminate the fundamental
parts of FBIM simulations in a Danish context, i.e. the initial intervention stages of the
investigation and initiation phase and the main intervention phase.
For these purposes, four experiments have been successfully conducted and documented. During
the first three experiments, the 27 firefighting activities, conducted by Danish firefighters, were
documented. During the fourth experiment, eight milestones of the fire scenario were identified
and documented as a measure of validity for distinct elements in FBIM.
As a secondary objective in this project, to enable easy and fast FBIM simulation, a digital
representation has been successfully developed. With some limitations, the developed program
represents the FBIM charts and dataset and can be tailored to fit most cases. The developed
software has played an essential part in the model validation of this project by enabling a
manageable and transparent simulation platform. It is expected that the availability of an
appropriate digital representation of FBIM will be advantageous for any future study related to
FBIM.
The experiments, conducted in this project, are associated with scarce sample pools, inadequate
for an accurate statistical representation and analysis. Therefore, only qualitative assessments
and indicative validations can be justified. Utilising a relatively crude acceptance criterion,
which has been deemed appropriate for an indicative validation, the 27 activities have been
successfully assessed. By the measure of relative error, if available, each of the documented
94
Firefighter Engineering - Validation of the Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
==PAGE:102==
activities has been compared to FBIM counterparts. Thus, the comparison of the documented
mean values and those equivalent provided by FBIM is utilised as a guideline in the assessment
and validation.
Among the 27 activities, 10 were included with the intention to validate corresponding FBIM
counterparts. Three of these have been deemed indicatively validated, i.e. the activities:
P2, Q2, and Q3. A significant compliance, to the conservative side, has been documented,
suggesting that these activities are well represented by FBIM. The last seven are associated
with too large discrepancies between the mean values, for them to be considered indicatively
validated. Out of these seven, the results of the four activities: O1, O1, T5, and Y2, indicate
the largest discrepancies. In general, the results indicate conservative estimations, except for
Q1, which is indicated to be significantly underestimating.
The remaining 17 activities, documented in this project, were included with the intention
to implement and outline activities, not represented in FBIM. The results of four of these
indicatively validate their closest FBIM counterparts, i.e. the activities: V1 DK, V4.1 DK,
V4.2 DK, and V4.3 DK. This suggests that there is no significant difference when charging
Ø65- and Ø38-hoses compared to B- and C-hoses. Moreover, contradicting expectations,
the results suggest that V1 DK are represented by V1.2 from FBIM, despite their inherent
differences. Among the 17 activities, six of them are associated with too large discrepancies
between the mean values, for them to indicatively validate their closest FBIM counterparts. For
the remaining seven, no apparent FBIM counterparts are available, and thus no assessment is
performed. In general, the results indicate that, if used, the FBIM counterparts underestimate
the activities, except for T1.2 DK, T7 DK, and V1 DK, which is indicated to be conservative.
This supports the hypothesis that it would be advantageous to implement many of the given
activities in a Danish FBIM version.
The milestones in the fire scenario of the fourth experiment were successfully documented. Three
corresponding FBIM simulation cases with subtle differences were successfully implemented
in the developed software, by which the simulation results were obtained. The documented
and simulated results of each milestone were compared and assessed. The most significant
discrepancy was identified in the fifth milestone, reflecting the time for SHT 1, to enter the
premises, and reach the fire compartment. Across all simulation cases, the results indicate that
FBIM significantly underestimates this process, indicating that FBIM fails to represent this
activity with respect to the documented fire scenario.
Simulation case 2, has successfully served to illustrate that omitting the laying and charging
of the HP-hose completely and utilising primary search, cannot be assumed applicable with
respect to the documented fire scenario. Similarly, simulation case 1 has served to illustrate
that V2.2 might be considered applicable to describe the laying and charging of the HP-
hose, especially when including V4.2. Moreover, it has illustrated that secondary search is
significantly conservative, although more accurate than primary search, with respect to the
documented fire scenario. Simulation case 3, utilising the obtained results of the data collection,
has served to illustrate significant compliance or improvements across four milestones, while
contradicting expectations with a significant worsening of two milestones, including the fifth
already mentioned. This suggests that by using the Danish data, the overall accuracy of FBIM
simulations can be enhanced and thus, applicable in a Danish setting.
By the findings of this project, the main conclusion is clear. At present, FBIM cannot be
validated in a Danish setting. To achieve the validation, more independent experiments need
to be conducted and documented similarly, but with more diversity, to those included in this
project. The size of the sample pools, of both the data collection and fire scenarios, needs to be
increased significantly, to describe the statistical distributions of the activities with appropriate
Firefighter Engineering - Validation of the Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
95
==PAGE:103==
accuracy. Based on this, a thorough statistical analysis can be performed, from which a
reasonable validation can be achieved. However, it can also be concluded that the findings
of this project illustrate the potential of FBIM by indicating that FBIM is indeed capable of
capturing elements of the intervention process with appropriate accuracy. This project has
illuminated several challenges and laid a pathway for the future development of FBIM in Danish
settings. Thereby, the objective of this project is considered fulfilled, despite not being able to
definitively validate FBIM as a whole in a Danish setting.
96
Firefighter Engineering - Validation of the Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
==PAGE:104==
Chapter 7
Future Work
During this project, several key learnings and insights have been obtained. To pass them on,
they are summarised in the following.
FBIM Applicability
In this stage of the FBIM development, it is suggested that FBIM is exclusively utilised
to compare designs, rather than to validate them. This implies that any future study and
application of FBIM is suggested to focus only on relative time estimates, comparing different
set-ups and evaluating how design choices impact the intervention process. There are still
aspects unaccounted for, why any form of intervention validation can be misleading. It is
further suggested, that the focus of future study is kept on the first three intervention phases
as described in this project. Until these phases are well accounted for, the end of intervention
phase is unimportant from the perspective of time estimation and intervention simulation.
Independent sample pool size
Any future work should consider increasing the sample pool sizes of the data utilised in FBIM.
This is required to obtain more accurate representations of the activities, and thus more accurate
simulation results. Moreover, the methodology of FBIM also requires further validation and
comparisons with different fire scenarios and intervention processes to ensure that the charts
and flow in between provide a valid representation. This could also be achieved by introducing
careful logs of real fire intervention processes, to which corresponding FBIM simulations can be
compared.
Generalisation of FBIM data tables
The findings of this project suggest the distinctions P3 DK, P4 DK, P5 DK, and P6 DK
might be unproductive. Therefore, it is suggested that any future work should consider further
generalisation of these activities. E.g. such that P1, P4 DK, P5 DK, and P6 DK are covered
by the same element, and P2 and P DK are covered by the same element. This is very similar
to the generalisation appearing in the FBIM dataset. Furthermore, it is suggested that any
future work should considered to redefine and streamline the activities in P and V, as there are
indications of overlap, etc. In much the same way, it is suggested that any future work should
consider extending the FBIM table of search and rescue, such that it can reflect a larger variety
of search techniques and rescue operations. Likewise, the activities of Tables M and N should
also be considered extended, to emphasize the distinctions of not donning BA, donning BA but
without a facemask, and donning BA with a facemask. As they are considered significantly
different, it is expected that the distinction will be advantageous, and could also outline the
individual activity of donning facemasks.
Firefighter Engineering - Validation of the Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
97
==PAGE:105==
Adjustment of FBIM Methodology
By the findings of this project, it is suggested that the FBIM charts should be further adjusted
and streamlined according to Danish procedures and tactics, for an ideal representation of
Danish intervention activities. This project has illuminated several challenges with the current
FBIM design, exclusively with respect to intervention simulation, and further development is
suggested to adjust the FBIM charts for better digital representation. Moreover, the findings
of this project warrant a better representation of the process of reaching the fire compartment,
through a series of other compartments. By the results of this project, this cannot be fully
accounted for by Tables Q and T.
98

Experiment Description - Experiment
2, 3 and 4
106

==PAGE:115==
 
 
2 
1. Introduktion 
Før anvendelsen af indsatsmodellen FBIM i dansk regi kan retfærdiggøres, ønskes datagrundlaget for 
modellen at blive undersøgt, tilpasset og valideret. Modellen er designet til brug i australske og 
newzealandske områder, og grundet forskelle i procedurer, taktikker, udstyr mv. kan mange af disse 
datasæt ikke forventes at kunne overføres direkte til brug i Danmark. Efter grundig overvejelse er en 
række af disse data blevet udvalgt til yderligere undersøgelse. Grundet projektets tidmæssige 
begrænsning, er der blevet lagt vægt på at indsamle data, som er grundlæggende for enhver brand- 
og redningsindsats, og som kan forventes at være betydelig anderledes i Danmark.  
 
Det anerkendes, at dataene indsamlet i denne undersøgelse vil være af betydelig lav population og 
dermed have et svagt statistisk grundlag. Denne undersøgelse kan derfor ikke anses for at være 
fyldestgørende, men snarere som et indledende skridt til at skabe et dansk data bibliotek, med 
opfordring til yderligere dataindsamling. 
 
Denne forsøgsbeskrivelse er lavet i forbindelse med DTU kandidat specialet: ’Validering af Fire 
Brigade Intervention Model for Dansk indsatsteknik’ og er udarbejdet af Michael B. Meincke i 
samarbejde med medstuderende Vladyslav V. Bogatyy, samt vejleder og lektor Anne S. Dederichs. 
Forsøgsplanen er udarbejdet for at beskrive og dokumentere forsøgsindholdet til forsøgsdeltagere og 
til fremtidig reference. Projektet omhandler blandt andet en analyse og indsamling af data for 
almindelige brand- og redningsopgaver, som danske brandmænd er uddannet og trænet i.  
 
Alle forsøg afholdes på brandøvelsespladsen i Københavns Lufthavn (se Fig. 1) i samarbejde med 
CARFA (Copenhagen Airport Rescue and Firefighting Academy) og lufthavnens beredskab: Airport 
Rescue and Firefighting. Forsøgene er derfor defineret ud fra de tilgængelige rammer og CARFA’s 
øvelsesbygning, der er baseret på 40 fods containere, og udføres af lufthavnens brandmænd fra hold 
3. Forsøgene afholdes i forbindelse med, at brandmændene er i beredskab, hvormed forstyrrelser i 
øvelsesafholdelsen kan forventes at forekomme og, at der samtidigt vil være stor fokus på at sikre og 
opretholde deres beredskab og responstider under udførelsen. I tilfælde af afbrydelser forventes det, 
at uafsluttede øvelser påbegyndes på ny. Øvelserne vil blive udført sekventielt i den nedenfor angivet 
rækkefølge i løbet af samme dag, d. 26/6 – 2024 i tidsrummet 9-16. Det fornødne brandmateriel, 
udstyr, armatur osv. for hver enkelt øvelse er vedlagt i appendiks. Det forudsættes, at læseren er 
bekendt med almindelig brandmandsterminologi og at disse ikke er nødvendige at definere (se evt. 
reference materiale). 
2. Formål 
Formålet med øvelserne er at observere, indsamle og om muligt, validere tidsmæssige værdier for en 
række processer, der er grundlæggende for danske brand- og redningsindsatser. Øvelserne er opdelt 
i tre hovedgrupper:  
1) Udvalgte standard udlægninger – Til indsamling af danske data 
2) Afsøgning- og redningsopgave – Til indsamling af danske data 
3) Brand scenarie – Til sammenligning med og validering af indsatsmodellen FBIM i dansk regi 
 
==PAGE:116==
 
 
3 
Øvelse 1 indebærer fire standard udlægninger, hvor de enkelte delprocesser er i fokus. Øvelse 2 
indebærer to afsøgnings- og redningsopgaver, hvor afsøgningshastigheder (areal per tid) ønskes 
bestemt med og uden brug af termisk kamera. Sekundært vil personredningshastigheden (afstand per 
tid) være i fokus. Øvelse 3 indebærer et større, men relativt simpelt brandscenarie til sammenligning 
med en tilsvarende FBIM-simulering. Alle øvelser afvikles så vidt muligt med en hastighed tilsvarende 
et reelt brandscenarie, dvs. med ’normal fire ground speed’.  
 
Det overordnede formål er desuden at etablere et grundlag og udgangspunkt for et data bibliotek til 
brug ved FBIM-simuleringer i Danmark.  
 
3. Øvelse 1 – Standard Udlægninger 
Den mest fundamentelle opgave, som skal udføres inden en egentlig brandsluknings- og/eller 
redningsoperation kan igangsættes, er etablering af angrebsudlægning og evt. vandforsyning. Der 
findes forskellige typer af standardudlægninger til anvendelse i forskellige situationer. Det ønskes, at 
disse standardudlægninger kan blive repræsenteret i indsatsmodellen FBIM, hvilket kræver 
etableringen af et tilsvarende datagrundlag.  
 
I dette projekt ønskes følgende fire standardudlægninger implementeret i indsatsmodellen: HT-
udlægning, B/C-udlægning, stigrørsudlægning og udvendig ophaling af C-angreb fra slangekurv. 
Disse er beskrevet i [1,2]. De udgør sammen med skumudlægning, ophaling af C-angreb med dobbelt 
Figur 1 – Skitseret overblik over dele af lufthavnens brandøvelsesplads med indklippet tegning af øvelsesbygningen. 
Kilde: Google MapsTM og tegning af øvelsesbygning (leveret af CARFA), sammensat af forfattere 
==PAGE:117==
 
 
4 
oprullede C-slanger, ophaling af HT-angreb samt udlægning af sugeslange, fundamentet for de mest 
almindelige danske brand- og redningsindsatser. Af tidsmæssige årsager er kun enkelte blevet 
udvalgt til at indgå i dette projekt.  
Forsøgsopstilling 
Alle fire følgende øvelser vil som udgangspunkt blive gennemført i henhold til procedurerne for de 
respektive udlægninger og med en 1+5 bemanding, dvs. én holdleder og fem brandmænd inkl. 
Motorpasser. Alle deltagere vil udføre øvelsen i fuld indsatsmundering. De fire brandmænd, der udgør 
røgdykkerhold 1 og 2, vil desuden bære røgdykkerapparat, dog uden masker.  
 
Udgangspunktet for øvelsernes begyndelse er, at det pågældende mandskab står klar, iklædt det 
nødvendige udstyr, ved autosprøjten, der står i tomgang med alle jalousiskabe lukket. Mandskabet er 
forinden begyndelsen informeret om deres individuelle opgaver samt øvelsens slutmål. Dette skyldes, 
at formålet med øvelserne er at måle på en række delprocesser, hvilket anses for at være upåvirket af 
dette faktum. Slutmålet for de fire følgende øvelser vil også være ens for at understøtte gode 
sammenligningsmuligheder. Slutmålet er defineret ved vandafgivelse af 1. røgdykkerhold på 2. sal af 
øvelsesbygningen (se evt. turkis markering i Figur 2). Markeringen med vand skal symbolisere, at 
røgdykkerholdet nu er klar til at trænge ind i bygningen, og at den egentlige indsats kan begynde.  
 
Figur 2 – Skitseret overblik over kamera placeringer og relevante distancer til 
øvelse 1. Kilde: sammensat af forfattere 
   
 
==PAGE:118==
 
 
5 
Dokumentation af tidsmålingerne af de udvalgte delprocesser for hver af de fire øvelser, vil ske vha. 
velplacerede kameraer. Optagelserne vil da senere blive analyseret for at bestemme de enkelte 
målinger og parametre. Placeringen af hvert kamera er angivet i øvelsesskitsen (se figur 2). De 
nødvendige afstandsmålinger o.l. vil løbende blive målt op for at sikre så nøjagtige resultater som 
muligt. 
Forsøgsudførelse  
Hver af de følgende fire øvelser vil have samme udgangspunkt for start- og slutkonfiguration, og 
benytte de samme kameraer til dokumentation. De vil kun blive afviklet én gang efter hinanden med 
en kort pause inkl. genetablering imellem. Udførelsen for hver af de enkelte øvelser er beskrevet 
nedenfor, men følger som udgangspunkt den generelle procedure beskrevet i [1,2]. 
 
Øvelse 1.a – HT-udlægning 
Forsøgsdeltagerene er samlet ved autosprøjten og når alle er klar, signaleres der klart og tydeligt at 
øvelsen påbegyndes.  
 
Trin 1:  
Nr. 1 fremtager SOS-oppakningen og begiver sig mod det forudbestemte setup område med 
strålerørsenden af HT-slangen. 
Nr. 2 og 3 hjælper med udrulningen af HT-slangen samt etableringen af slange-/manøvrebugter, indtil 
hele HT-slangen er rullet ud (90m). 
Nr. 4 fremtager BB-oppakningen samt to B-slangekurve, og udlægger fødeslange fra autosprøjten til 
brandhanen, inkl. skylning/flush af brandhanen.  
Motorpasseren betjener HT-slangevinden samt tager imod og tilkobler fødeslangen til autosprøjten. 
Figur 3 – TV.: Nr. 1, 2 og 3 ved HT-udlægning. Kilde: [1]. TH.: Skitse over HT-øvelsen. Grønt område indikerer 
set-up område, turkis område indikere slut område. Kilde: Forfattere 
     
 
==PAGE:119==
 
 
6 
Trin 2: 
Nr. 1 og 2 mødes ved det forudbestemte setup område, kalder vand frem med åbent strålerør, og 
kontrollerer strålerøret og -billedet.  
Nr. 3 og 4 begiver sig tilbage til autosprøjten og melder sig til holderen. 
Motorpasseren tryksætter HT-slangevinden ved signal fra nr. 1 og 2. 
Trin 3: 
Når strålerøret og -billedet er kontrolleret og evt. justeret, trækker røgdykkerholdet, bestående af nr. 1 
og 2, op ad tappen på anden sal. Her etableres et passende slangedepot, hvorefter de markerer med 
vand, at de er klar til at trænge ind og øvelsen er slut. 
 
Forsøgsdata: 
Følgende aktiviteter ønskes bestemt: 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage SOS-oppakning 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage BB-oppakning og to B-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge og tryksætte 90m HT-slange 
• 
Tiden det tager at skylle/flushe brandhane 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge, forbinde og tryksætte fødeslange 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 4 at begive sig tilbage til autosprøjten uden udstyr 
• 
Tiden det tager at begive sig op på 2. sal med HT-slange 
 
Øvelse 1.b – B/C-udlægning 
Forsøgsdeltagerne er samlet ved autosprøjten og når alle er klar, signalerer holdlederen klart og 
tydeligt at øvelsen påbegyndes. B/C-forgrener er forinden øvelsesstart placeret på det forudbestemte 
sted. 
Figur 4 – TV.: Nr. 1, 2 og 3 ved B/C-udlægning. Kilde: [1]. TH.: Skitse over B/C-øvelsen. Grønt område 
indikerer set-up område, blåt område indikere slut område. Kilde: Forfattere.  
==PAGE:120==
 
 
7 
Trin 1: 
Nr. 1 fremtager SOS-oppakningen samt en dobbelt oprullet C-slange, og begiver sig mod det 
forudbestemte set-up område. Her udlægges den dobbelt oprullede C-slange, og strålerør tilkobles.  
Nr. 2 fremtager to C-slangekurve og begiver sig mod den placerede B/C-forgrener. Her tilkobles og 
udlægges to C-slanger i passende slangebugter fra forgreneren til nr. 1, ved det forudbestemte setup 
område. 
Nr. 3 fremtager to B-slangekurve, udlægger én B-slange fra autosprøjten til forgreneren, kalder vand 
frem og betjener forgreneren. 
Nr. 4 fremtager BB-oppakningen samt to B-slangekurve, og udlægger fødeslange fra autosprøjten til 
brandhanen, inkl. skylning/flush af brandhanen.  
Motorpasseren tager imod og tilkobler både føde- og angrebsslangen til autosprøjten. Ved signal fra 
nr. 3, tryksætter motorpasseren angrebsslangen. 
Trin 2: 
Nr. 1 og 2 mødes ved det forudbestemte setup område, hvor de kobler hver deres medbragte C-
slanger sammen. Herefter kalder de vand frem med åbent strålerør, og strålerøret og -billedet 
kontrolleres.  
Nr. 3 tryksætter angrebsudløbet ved signal fra nr. 1 og 2. 
Nr. 4 begiver sig tilbage til autosprøjten og melder sig til holderen. 
Motorpasseren betjener fortsat pumpen og sørger for det fornødne vandtryk ved strålerøret. 
Trin 3: 
Når strålerøret og -billedet er kontrolleret og evt. justeret, trækker røgdykkerholdet, bestående af nr. 1 
og 2, op ad tappen på anden sal. Her etableres et passende slangedepot, hvorefter de markerer med 
vand, at de er klar til at trænge ind, og øvelsen er slut. 
 
Forsøgsdata: 
Følgende aktiviteter ønskes bestemt: 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage SOS-oppakning inkl. dobbelt oprullet C-slange 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage to C-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage to B-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage BB-oppakning og to B-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at skylle/flushe brandhane 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge, forbinde og tryksætte fødeslange 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 4 at begive sig tilbage til autosprøjten uden udstyr 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge og forbinde B-slanger fra sprøjte til forgrener 
• 
Tiden det tager at tryksætte B-slanger fra sprøjte til forgrener 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 2 at begive sig til forgreneren med to C-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge og forbinde C-slanger fra forgrener til strålerør 
• 
Tiden det tager at tryksætte C-slanger fra forgrener til strålerør 
• 
Tiden det tager at begive sig op på 2. sal med C-slange 
 
 
==PAGE:121==
 
 
8 
Øvelse 1.c – Stigrørsudlægning 
Forsøgsdeltagerne er samlet ved 
autosprøjten, og når alle er klar, signalerer 
holdlederen klart og tydeligt at øvelsen 
påbegyndes.  
 
Trin 1: 
Nr. 1 og 2 fremtager hver en 
højhusoppakning (30m C-slange pakket på 
en særlig måde, inkl. strålerør, C/C forgrener 
og en 1m C-slange), og begiver sig mod det 
forudbestemte setup område på 2. sal. Her 
udlægges højhusoppakningen og tilkobles 
det lukkede stigrørsudløb og strålerør. 
Nr. 3 fremtager en B-slangekurv, samt 
stigrørsstykke, udlægger én B-slange fra 
autosprøjten til stigrørsindløbet. Her 
påsættes stigrørsstykket, og der kaldes vand 
frem. Derefter udlægges endnu en B-slange 
fra stigrøret til autosprøjten. 
Nr. 4 fremtager BB-oppakningen samt to B-
slangekurve, og udlægger fødeslange fra 
autosprøjten til brandhanen, inkl. skylning/flush af brandhanen.  
Motorpasseren tager imod og tilkobler både føde- og stigrørsslanger til autosprøjten. Ved signal fra nr. 
3, tryksætter motorpasseren stigrørsslangen. Ved modtagelse af den anden B-slange fra stigrøret 
tryksættes denne også. 
Trin 2: 
Når nr. 1 og 2 er færdige med deres klargøring af angrebsslangen, åbner nr. 2 for stigrørsventilen og 
højhusoppakningen tryksættes med åbent strålerør. Derefter kontrolleres strålerøret og -billedet.  
Nr. 3 og 4 begiver sig tilbage til autosprøjten og melder sig til holderen (kontrol af ubenyttede 
stigrørsventiler er i dette tilfælde ikke relevant). 
Motorpasseren betjener fortsat pumpen og sørger for det fornødne vandtryk ved strålerøret. 
Trin 3: 
Når strålerøret og -billedet er kontrolleret og evt. justeret, markerer røgdykkerholdet, bestående af nr. 
1 og 2, med vand, at de er klar til at trænge ind, hvormed øvelsen er slut. 
 
Forsøgsdata: 
Følgende aktiviteter ønskes bestemt: 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage højhusoppakning 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage en B-slangekurv, samt stigrørsstykke 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage BB-oppakning og to B-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at skylle/flushe brandhane 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge, forbinde og tryksætte fødeslange 
Figur 5 – Skitse over stigrørs-øvelsen. Grønt område indikerer set-
up område, blåt område indikere slut område. Kilde: Forfattere. 
==PAGE:122==
 
 
9 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 4 at begive sig tilbage til autosprøjten uden udstyr 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge og forbinde B-slanger fra sprøjte til stigrørsstykke 
• 
Tiden det tager at tryksætte B-slanger fra sprøjte til stigrørs-indløb 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 1 og 2 at begive sig til 2. sal med højhusoppakning 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge og forbinde højhusoppakning fra stigrørs-udløb til strålerør 
• 
Tiden det tager at tryksætte C-slanger fra stigrørs-udløb til strålerør 
 
Øvelse 1.d – Udvendig ophaling af C-angreb fra Slangekurv 
Forsøgsdeltagerene er samlet ved autosprøjten og når alle er klar, signalerer holdlederen klart og 
tydeligt at øvelsen påbegyndes. Denne øvelse er en variant af B/C-udlægningen, og B/C-forgreneren 
er forinden øvelsesstart placeret på forudbestemte sted tæt ved ophalingsstedet. 
 
Trin 1: 
Nr. 1 fremtager SOS-oppakningen samt en dobbelt oprullet C-slange, og begiver sig mod det 
forudbestemte setup område på 2. sal. Her udlægges den dobbelt oprullede C-slange, og strålerør 
tilkobles. Derudover fastgøres ophalelinen, hvorefter ophalingsposen kastes ned til ophalingsstedet. 
Nr. 2 fremtager to C-slangekurve, tilkobler C-slange til forgreneren og begiver sig mod ophalingsstedet 
med begge slangekurve. Her fastgøres ophalelinen til slangen fra den ubenyttede slangekurv og der 
signaleres til nr. 1 at ophalingen kan begynde. 
Nr. 3 fremtager to B-slangekurve, udlægger to B-slanger fra autosprøjten til forgreneren, kalder vand 
frem og betjener forgreneren. 
Nr. 4 fremtager BB-oppakningen samt to B-slangekurve, og udlægger fødeslange fra autosprøjten til 
brandhanen, inkl. skylning/flush af brandhanen.  
Motorpasseren tager imod og tilkobler både føde- og angrebsslangen til autosprøjten. Ved signal fra 
nr. 3, tryksætter motorpasseren angrebsslangen. 
Figur 6 – TV.: Nr. 2 ved ophalingsstedet. Kilde: [1]. TH.: Skitse over ophalings-øvelsen. Grønt område indikerer set-
up område, blåt område indikere slut område. Kilde: Forfattere.  
  
 
==PAGE:123==
 
 
10 
Trin 2: 
Nr. 1 haler slanger op mens nr. 2 styrer slangen fra ophalingsstedet. Når der er ophalet en hel 
slangelængde, standses ophalingen. Nr. 2 tilkobler så den ophalede slange med slangen som er 
forbundet til forgreneren, og ophalingen genoptages således, at der er to slangelængder ml. 
forgreneren og nr. 1. Herefter fastgør nr. 1 den ophalede slange med en slangekrog, og tilkobler sin 
dobbelt oprullede slange. Der er nu tre C-slanger mellem forgrener og strålerør.  
Nr. 4 begiver sig tilbage til autosprøjten og melder sig til holdlederen. 
Trin 3: 
Når ophalingen er færdiggjort, begiver nr. 2 sig op til nr. 1. Efter slangerne er placeret 
hensigtsmæssigt, kaldes vandet frem med åbent strålerør, hvorefter strålerør og -billedet kontrolleres. 
Nr. 3 tryksætter angrebsudløbet ved signal fra nr. 1 og 2. 
Motorpasseren betjener fortsat pumpen og sørger for det fornødne vandtryk ved strålerøret. 
Trin 4: 
Når strålerøret og -billedet er kontrolleret og evt. justeret, markerer røgdykkerholdet, bestående af nr. 
1 og 2, med vand, at de er klar til at trænge ind, hvormed øvelsen er slut. 
 
Forsøgsdata: 
Følgende aktiviteter ønskes bestemt: 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage SOS-oppakning inkl. dobbelt oprullet C-slange 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage to C-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage to B-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at fremtage BB-oppakning og to B-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at skylle/flushe brandhane 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge, forbinde og tryksætte fødeslange 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 4 at begive sig tilbage til autosprøjten uden udstyr 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge og forbinde B-slanger fra sprøjte til forgrener 
• 
Tiden det tager at tryksætte B-slanger fra sprøjte til forgrener 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 1 at begive sig til setup området på 2. sal 
• 
Tiden det tager for nr. 2 at begive sig til forgreneren med to C-slangekurve 
• 
Tiden det tager at lægge, ophale og forbinde C-slanger 
• 
Tiden det tager at tryksætte C-slanger fra forgrener til strålerør 
• 
Tiden det tager at begive sig op på 2. sal uden udstyr 
4. Øvelse 2 – Afsøgning og Personredning 
En anden elementær opgave ifm. danske brand- og redningsindsatser, er processen for afsøgning og 
personredning i røgfyldt lokale med lav sigtbarhed. Inspireret af AFAC’s FBIM-øvelse for ’search and 
rescue’ (se appendiks) opstilles der her tilsvarende øvelser for at bestemme afsøgningshastigheden 
(areal per tid), samt personredningshastigheden (afstand per tid). Det ønskes at validere dataene fra 
FBIM samtidig med at implementere muligheden for anvendelsen af termisk kamera til at understøtte 
og optimere afsøgningsprocessen. Anvendelsen af termisk kamera ifm. afsøgningsopgaver i Danmark 
anses for at være relativt almindeligt, og det forventes at øge afsøgningshastigheden betydeligt.  
 
==PAGE:124==
 
 
11 
Afsøgningsoperationer er en relativ kompleks proces at beskrive, den afhænger markant af rummet 
som ønskes afsøgt, i form af størrelse, udformning, møblering og ventilationsmuligheder. Processen 
afhænger også af brand- og røgudbredelsen der dikterer bevægelsesmulighederne for røgdykkerne, 
baseret på varme og sigtbarhed, og som kan forsinke afsøgningen, idet det ofte er nødvendigt først at 
slå branden ned og køle røggasserne. Naturligvis vil processen også afhænge af personerne fundet 
under afsøgningen, da disse skal bringes i sikkerhed hurtigst muligt, hvormed afsøgningen vil blive 
afbrudt. I praksis, er det endnu ikke muligt at afdække og repræsentere disse faktorer med enkelte 
afsøgningshastigheder, hvormed det er nødvendigt at simplificere processen betydeligt. 
 
I dette projekt opstilles to identiske og simple øvelser for afsøgning og personredning, hvoraf den ene 
udføres uden termisk kamera og den anden med termisk kamera. I begge øvelser vil der også indgå 
horisontal personredning, simuleret vha. øvelsesdukke. 
Forsøgsopstilling 
De to på hinanden følgende øvelser vil som udgangspunkt blive gennemført i henhold til proceduren 
for afsøgning og personredning, beskrevet i [1,3]. Hver øvelse vil blive udført af to forskellige 
røgdykkerhold, som forhindres i intern kommunikation mellem øvelserne for at undgå forhåndsviden. 
Alle deltagere vil udføre øvelsen i fuld indsatsmundering inkl. røgdykkerapparat med anlagt masker. 
For at simulere en reel afsøgningsoperation udstyres røgdykkerholdet med en HT-slange og 
øvelsesbygningen vil være mørklagt og røgfyldt.  
 
Det primære formål med øvelserne er at bestemme afsøgningshastighederne med og uden brug af 
termisk kamera i form af areal per tid. Ud over afsøgningstiden, kræver dette en bestemmelse af det 
afsøgte areal, hvilket vil være forsøgets største udfordring. For at imødekomme dette, benyttes interne 
termiske kameraer til at følge røgdykkerholdet og dermed til at kunne estimere det afsøgte areal. 
Endvidere følges røgdykkerholdet inde i øvelsesbygningen af en observatør, som dokumenterer 
processen ved at filme et termisk kamera. Forsøget er således også dokumenteret vha. 
kameraoptagelser.  
 
Forsøgsopstillingen er skitseret i figur 7, hvori det ses at afsøgningsområdet er opdelt i forskellige 
zoner. Dette er gjort for at understøtte estimeringen af afsøgningsarealet. Endvidere ses placeringen 
af interne kameraer med lilla firkanter og øvelsesdukken med orange cirkel, som placeres skjult fra 
døråbningen. Desuden er afsøgningsruten også markeret. Afsøgningszonerne er baseret på en 
antagelse om, at et røgdykkerhold tilsammen kan afdække en bredde på ca. 2.4m vinkelret på 
afsøgningsretningen, dvs. ca. 1.2m per brandmand inkl. eventuelle overlap, hvilket vurderes til at være 
realistisk - denne værdi er primært fastsat ud fra bredden af containerne. Hver zone markeres op 
således, at de er mulige at identificere fra optagelserne. 
 
Orange zone forventes at være hurtigt afsøgt grundet lyset fra indtrængningsdøren og rummets lille 
størrelse, og vil derfor ikke indgå i dataindsamlingen. Gul zone, som repræsenterer en tom korridor, vil 
også være oplyst fra indtrængningsvejen, men i betydelig mindre grad. Korridorens simple udformning 
gør, at der også her forventes en højere afsøgningshastighed, som dog vil blive korrigeret og 
forlænget af overlap i afsøgningen, der skyldes afsøgningsretningen i korridoren. Gul zone vil derfor 
medtages i dataindsamlingen. Blå, lilla, rød, og mørkeblå zone, forventes derimod at være helt 
==PAGE:125==
 
 
12 
mørklagt. Dette sammen med rummenes udformning betyder, at disse zoner forventes at have de 
laveste afsøgningshastigheder, til trods for, at der kun vil forekomme få overlap i afsøgningen.  
Blå zone repræsenterer et tomt stykke af et større rum, lilla zone et tomt stykke af et større rum med 
kompleks udformning og få objekter, rød zone et tomt stykke af et større rum med en trappeopgang 
og mørkeblå zone repræsenterer et tomt stykke af et større rum med en del objekter. Således vil 
dataindsamlingen også være baseret på disse zoner.  
Forsøgsudførelse 
Udgangspunktet for hver øvelse vil være ens, og benytte de samme kameraer til dokumentation. De 
vil kun blive afviklet én gang efter hinanden med en kort pause og genetablering imellem. Ved 
øvelsernes begyndelse, vil deltagerne stå klar ved indtrængningspunktet, dvs. døren til 
øvelsesbygningen, iført deres nødvendige udstyr, inkl. anlagt maske og udlagt HT-slange i passende 
slangebugter. Desuden er røgdykkerholdet instrueret i afsøgningsretningen (venstre om) og HT-
slangen vil blive lempet i døren.  
 
Øvelse 2.a – Afsøgning og personredning uden termisk kamera - Forsøgsdata: 
Følgende aktiviteter ønskes bestemt: 
• 
Tiden det tager at afsøge hver zone, inkl. etablering af passende slangedepoter m.v. 
• 
Tiden det tager at udfri øvelsesdukken 
Figur 7 – Oversigt over afsøgningsøvelse og zone inddeling i farver. Lilla kasse indikerer interne kameraer, Orange 
cirkel indikerer øvelsesdukke. Kilde: Tegning af øvelsesbygning (leveret af CARFA), redigeret af forfattere 
==PAGE:126==
 
 
13 
Øvelse 2.b – Afsøgning og personredning med termisk kamera - Forsøgsdata: 
Følgende aktiviteter ønskes bestemt: 
• 
Tiden det tager at afsøge hver zone, inkl. etablering af passende slangedepoter m.v. 
• 
Tiden det tager at udfri øvelsesdukken 
5. Øvelse 3 – Brandscenarie 
Den sidste øvelse, som ønskes afviklet, er opstillet til at simulere et brandscenarie fra ankomst til 
brandstedet, til at brandsluknings- og redningsoperationerne er afviklet. Scenariet vil indeholde mange 
af de foregående undersøgte aktiviteter og forventes at repræsentere en mere realistisk og 
fuldstændig brand- og redningsindsats. Formålet med øvelsen er at muliggøre en tilsvarende 
simulering med indsatsmodellen FBIM, hvormed en evaluering og validering af selve modellen og 
dens opbygning vil være mulig.  
 
Øvelsen vil derfor blive udformet således at de to midterste faser (ud af fire) i en generel brand- og 
redningsindsats er repræsenteret i varieret omfang. De fire faser er beskrevet i [1] og betegnes ved: 
(1) præinterventions fasen, (2) rekognoscering og igangsættelsesfasen, (3) hovedinterventions fasen, 
og (4) den afsluttende fase. Fase 1 og 2 indeholder dermed alle interventionsaktiviteterne fra ankomst 
til brandsluknings- og redningsoperationer. Alt efter brandens størrelse og indsatsens omfang, vil 
brandsluknings- og redningsoperationerne fortsætte over i den afsluttende fase. Dette er især hvis 
mandskabet og ressourcerne i første indsatsen ikke er tilstrækkelige, og der er behov for udskiftning 
af røgdykkere eller rekvirering af yderligere ressourcer for at afslutte indsatsen. 
 
Denne øvelse vil indeholde følgende elementer:  
• 
Holdleder kommunikerer med brandvagt og bestemmer brandens lokation og antal savnede 
personer 
• 
Holdleder udsteder ordre og igangsætter mandskabet 
• 
Holdleder udpeger indtrængningsvejen (ens for begge røgdykkerhold) 
• 
Røgdykkerhold 1 etablerer stigrørs udlægning med højhusoppakning 
• 
Røgdykkerhold 2 etablerer vandforsyning fra hydrant og til stigrørssystemet 
• 
Røgdykkerhold 1 indsættes direkte på branden 
• 
Holdleder rekognoscerer og vurderer branden (via. en perimeter gang rundt om bygningen (fra 
og til setup området) 
• 
Efter at have afsluttet deres primære opgave, indsættes røgdykkerhold 2 til afsøgning og 
redning (uden termisk kamera), udstyret med en HT-slange 
• 
Efter endt afsøgning- og redningsoperation indsættes røgdykkerhold 2 til branden 
• 
Scenariet afsluttes når der er to strålerør på den givne brand.  
Forsøgsopstilling 
Dette forsøg vil blive afviklet som et reelt brandscenarie. Der vil derfor være mange ting der vil ske 
samtidigt og mange detaljer, som ønskes dokumenteret. Derfor vil der her blive lagt vægt på brugen af 
velplaceret kameraer til en senere analyse. Der vil både anvendes udvendige og indvendige 
kameraer, samt observatører udstyret med kameraer til at følge hvert røgdykkerhold inde i 
øvelsesbygningen. 
==PAGE:127==
 
 
14 
 
For at understøtte den efterfølgende FBIM-simulering er det nødvendigt, at enkelte rammer 
bestemmes og sikres. Disse består af følgende elementer: 
• 
Placeringen af autosprøjte  
• 
Type af slange udlægninger 
• 
Setup område, slangevej og indtrængningsvej  
• 
Brandens lokation og udbredelse 
• 
Afsøgningszoner 
De forskellige afstande, som skal bruges i FBIM simuleringen, vil blive estimeret ud fra disse rammer 
efter øvelsen er afviklet og ved brug af lasermåler. Blev de fastlagt forinden, ville det kræve at 
mandskabets bevægelser skulle styres og guides efter disse mål. Det vurderes, at det vil forstyrre 
øvelsesafviklingen i en betydelig grad, hvormed kun de mest overordnet rammer er fastsat. 
 
Forsøgsforløbet er skitseret i figurerne 8, 9 og 10, og simulerer et brand scenarie i en P-kælder, hvor 
der er gået brand i en elbil. Det benyttede brandmandsarmatur og udstyr er angivet i appendiks og vil 
ikke være en del af beredskabet, men ligge som ekstra udstyr på køretøjerne. Dermed kan 
beredskabet understøttes ved ”kun” at afkoble slangerne til autosprøjtren og køre afsted. 
Mandskabets skarpe røgdykkeraparater vil også stadig være tilgængelige i deres respektive køretøjer.  
Figur 8 – Oversigt over brand scenariets første angrebsudlægning. De grønne zoner markerer set-up området for 
hvert røgdykkerhold. Kilde: Tegning af øvelsesbygning (leveret af CARFA), redigeret af forfattere 
 
==PAGE:128==
 
 
15 
Forsøgsudførelse 
Udgangspunktet for øvelsen er en 1+5 bemanding, der alle er samlet ved autosprøjten ved øvelsens 
begyndelse. Holdlederen er forinden informeret om hvilke slange udlægninger og hvilken 
indtrængningsvej, der skal benyttes samt hvilke grundlæggende elementer indsatsen skal indeholde. 
Når alle forsøgsdeltagere er klar og iført deres udstyr, signaleres det klart og tydeligt at øvelsen 
begyndes.  
 
Trin 1: 
Holdleder kommunikerer med brandvagten 
Holdleder briefer og igangsætter sit mandskab 
Trin 2: 
Røgdykker hold 1 etablerer stigrørsudlægningen og indsættes direkte på branden 
Røgdykker hold 2 etablerer vandforsyningen til autosprøjten og til stigrørssystemet 
Holdleder rekognoscerer brandstedet 
Trin 3: 
Røgdykkerhold 1 finder frem til branden, slår den ned og sørger for at branden holdes under kontrol 
Røgdykkerhold 2 etablerer en HT-udlægning og indsættes til afsøgning og personredning 
Trin 4: 
Når afsøgningen er fuldført, indsættes røgdykkerhold 2 også på branden, hvormed brandslukning 
processen begyndes og scenariet afsluttes.   
Figur 9 – Oversigt over brand scenariets anden angrebsudlægning. De grønne zoner markerer set-up området for 
hvert røgdykkerhold. Kilde: Tegning af øvelsesbygning (leveret af CARFA), redigeret af forfattere 
 
==PAGE:129==

Proforma - Exercise 5 - FBIM - Version 2 
Exercise 5 Search and rescue 
 
Introduction  
This exercise is part of a series which have been developed to obtain specific statistical data, 
to ensure that necessary provisions are incorporated in building design for fire brigade 
operational tasks, and to ensure fire fighter safety.  Search and rescue is the most essential 
component of the data collection requirements and this exercise should be treated as a 
priority.  The information will be collated for input into a fire brigade model for effective 
brigade activities at time of fire.  While the activities listed may not exactly correspond to 
events on a fire ground, they have been designed for general coverage and maximum 
flexibility of data.  It is acknowledged that on the fire ground, some activities may be 
undertaken simultaneously, and an additional option is provided to complete the activities as a 
single exercise in real time if desired.  The exercises should not be considered as a 
competitive assessment, but normal fire ground speed is required.  No indication of the 
brigade (except brigade type as per AIRS standard) or station is to be included on the activity 
time sheet.  
 
Drill  
All fire fighters to be dressed in full turnout gear, including BA with obscured face mask, in 
blacked out room or large space to simulate heavy smoke logging conditions.  A 2 member team 
shall conduct a search of the room/space using either perimeter based or area based search 
techniques depending on the size of the room/space.  Typical furnishings and/or fixtures and 
contents are required to be randomly placed in the room/space.  Any rest periods necessary during 
the exercise (eg. due to ascending stairs) should be taken and recorded.  
 
Resources  
• 2 Search teams consisting of 2 people in full turnout gear and BA  
• Guide Lines  
• Adult size dummy  
• Obscured face masks (eg sand blasted) so that torch glow is apparent   
• Blacked out room/spaces of various sizes  
 
Objective to determine the time taken to:  
• conduct an internal search in smoke filled conditions  
• retrieve an incapacitated victim  
• travel in a smoke logged environment both horizontally and vertically  
• establish the size of a search area when a perimeter based search is no longer applicable and 
other procedures (eg guide lines) are required  
 
Method  
It should be possible to conduct this exercise in a variety of locations (preferably off station after 
prior arrangement with building owners) as obscured face masks are being used in lieu instead of 
smoke.  The procedures should be conducted in typically furnished occupancies so as to replicate 
==PAGE:132==
 
 
19 
real life situations.  As many types of buildings as possible should be utilised, large and small, for 
example offices, shops, warehouses, factories, hospitals, theatres, apartments, hotels, etc.  
  
The officer in charge shall note the times from entry into enclosure until exit from enclosure with 
any necessary comments as deemed appropriate.  
 
 
Task 1   
search of smoke logged area  
• please provide a sketch of each enclosure searched including dimensions and location of doors, 
furnishings, and other obstructions or points of interest; eg:  
  
  
  
• conduct a search appropriate to the size of the room/space as per usual procedures (indicate if 
guide lines used)  
  
NB  
If search of area is incomplete due to BA duration, indicate on the diagram what area has 
been searched.  The task must be completed with team of 2 firefighters and where possible 
repeated with multiple teams.  
 
Task 2   
simulated rescue of victim  
• position an adult size dummy (victim) to be rescued a measured distance remote from the 
enclosure exit point  
• send in a different search team to that which completed task 1 and record area searched until 
victim located  
• record time to locate dummy, time to remove dummy once found, and measure actual distance 
travelled in removing dummy to the exit  
==PAGE:133==
 
 
20 
 
Task 3   
vertical movement  
record the time taken for 2 firefighters, wearing BA with obscured face masks, to carry a high rise 
pack or similar to:  
• ascend, and  
• descend  
a recorded number of steps or treads (risers) NB 
 A typical case would be 3 flights of stairs.  
 
Notes for the Officer in charge  
It becomes very difficult to write down all the times if the whole drill is carried out as at a fire 
scene.  So much happens at once.  If attempting to work as at a fire scene, times for some 
activities will be missed whilst writing down the times of other activities.  It is therefore 
necessary to break down the process into manageable steps.  
  
All times are to be recorded in seconds.  A completed sample of exercise 5 provides an 
example of how the times should be recorded.  In the sample, the start time is recorded as zero 
on those occasions that the officer needed to stage the drill in manageable sections.  Note that 
the comments are necessary to clarify issues, such as the way the dummy was removed.  
  
It is necessary to use a different crew in task 2, because the crew in task 1 already has a 
familiarity with the enclosure.  Realistic times for search and rescue are essential for the data.  
  
It is important that the drill be carried out and should not be cancelled because of unforseen 
difficulties which may be faced in conducting the drill.  The officer should comment on any 
issue which caused a variation to the drill or affected recorded times.  Only the activity time 
sheet with the recorded times need be sent in.

def B4(self):

DEPENDENT!!
109

111

113

116

idx+1])
117   
ui1 = [x.strip() for x in eval(self.user_input_list[self.idx])]
118   
ui2 = [x.strip() for x in eval(self.user_input_list[self.idx+1])]
119   
120   
if len(ui1)!=len(ui2):
121   
print("Number of types and attacks must be the same!")
122   
return 0
123   
124   
125   
## IMPLEMENTER EN COUNTER FOR AT KUNNE OPDATERE/LOOPE!!
126   
a={}
127   
for i in range(len(ui1)):
128   
a[i]=int(ui1[i])*int(ui2[i])
129   
self.Vtot+=a[i]
130   
131   
## Konversion factor from FBIM ## L/min/kW
132   
K = 3/80
133   
134   
## Extinguishing Capacity:
135   
self.Qw = self.Vtot/K
136   
137   
self.idx += 2

)

22   # Initial determination of fire location 
23   chart5 = Chart5.Chart_5(time=0, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart5_Exp3.txt","main_exp3/Chart6_Exp3.txt"])
24   labels.append('Chart 5 - OIC')
25   start_vals.append(0)
26   dur_vals.append(chart5.time)
27   
28   milestones['Determination of fire location'] = [chart5.time]
29   
30   
31   # Relay and Receive (RAR) Orders 
32   RAR = 60+chart5.time
33   labels.append('Relay and Receive Orders')
34   start_vals.append(chart5.time)
35   dur_vals.append(RAR-chart5.time)
36   
37   milestones['Relay & Receive Orders'] = [RAR]
38   
39   # Assess fire 
40   chart7 = Chart7.Chart_7(time=RAR, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart7_Exp3.txt"])
41   milestones['OIC - Time to asses fire scene'] = [chart7.time]
42   
43   labels.append('Chart 7 - OIC')
44   start_vals.append(RAR)
45   dur_vals.append(chart7.time-RAR)
46   
47   
48   
49   # #%% Main Intervention Phase (chart 8 + 10 + 12 + 13 + 15)
50   
51   # Travel to set-up area - splitting in SHT's

"main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1.txt"]) # SHT 1
53   
54   labels.append('Chart 8 - SHT 1')
55   start_vals.append(RAR)
56   dur_vals.append(chart8_1.time-RAR)
57

59   chart8_21 = Chart8.Chart_8(time=RAR, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart8_Exp3_21.txt","main_exp3/Chart6_Exp3_21.txt"]) # 
FF3   
60   chart8_22 = Chart8.Chart_8(time=RAR, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart8_Exp3_22.txt","main_exp3/Chart6_Exp3_22.txt"]) # 
FF4

64   dur_vals.append(chart8_21.time-RAR)
65   
66   labels.append('Chart 8 - FF4, SHT 2')
67   start_vals.append(RAR)
68   dur_vals.append(chart8_22.time-RAR)
69   
70   # Time to set up water - SHT 1
71   chart10_1 = Chart10.Chart_10(time=chart8_1.time, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart10_Exp3_1.txt",
"main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_1.txt"])
72   
73   # Time to set up water - SHT 2
74   # Splitting up SHT 2 in FF3 and FF4 
75   chart10_21 = Chart10.Chart_10(time=chart8_21.time, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart10_Exp3_21.txt",
"main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_21.txt"]) # FF 3
76   chart10_22 = Chart10.Chart_10(time=chart8_22.time, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart10_Exp3_22.txt",
"main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_22.txt"]) # FF 4
77

80   if chart10_21.time<chart10_22.time: # FF 3 is done before FF 4
81   
current_time = chart10_22.time
82   
83   
labels.append('Chart 10 - SHT 2  (FF 3 waits)')
84   
start_vals.append(chart8_22.time)
85   
dur_vals.append(chart10_22.time-chart8_22.time)
86   
87   else:
# FF 4 is done before FF 3 
88   
current_time = chart10_21.time
89   
90   
labels.append('Chart 10 - SHT 2 (FF 4 waits)')
91   
start_vals.append(chart8_21.time)
92   
dur_vals.append(chart10_21.time-chart8_21.time)
93   
94   milestones['SHT 2 - Water Connection Established'] = [current_time]
95   
96   # Checking that water connection is established (FF 3) before SHT 1 moves to fire compartment!

done
99   
100   chart9_2 = Chart9.Chart_9(time=0, input_file="main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_21.txt")
101   FF3_water = chart10_21.time - chart9_2.time
# The acc. time where FF 3 has established water connection
102   
103   
104   if SHT1_water<FF3_water: # FF 3 is not done before SHT1 is ready to move to fire compartment - SHT 1 needs to wait

SHT1_water = FF3_water + chart9_1.time # The new 'chart10_1.time'
106

labels.insert(4,'Chart 10 - SHT 1 (w/ wait) \n 1. Attack Line')

113

116   
start_vals.insert(4,chart8_1.time)
117   
dur_vals.insert(4,chart10_1.time-chart8_1.time)
118

milestones['SHT 1 - Attack Line Established'] = [SHT1_water]

milestones['SHT 1 - Fire Control Initiated'] = [chart10_1.time]

"main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_2.txt"])
131   ## No HP hose i available in tabel V!?
132   
133   labels.append('Chart 10 - SHT 2 \n 2. Attack Line')
134   start_vals.append(current_time)

136   milestones['SHT 2 - Attack Line Established'] = [chart10_2.time]
137   
138   
139   # SHT 2 now perform S&R:
140   chart12 = Chart12.Chart_12(time=chart10_2.time, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart12_Exp3_2.txt"])
141   
142   milestones['SHT 2 - S&R Complete'] = [chart12.time]
143   labels.append('Chart 12 - SHT 2')
144   start_vals.append(chart10_2.time)
145   dur_vals.append(chart12.time-chart10_2.time)

165   
166   # Create text file of milestones, and durations
167   with open("case_1.txt", 'w') as f:
168   
for key, value in milestones.items():
169   
f.write('%s: %s sec \n' % (key, int(np.round(value[0]))))
170   
f.write('\n')
171   
for i in range(0,len(dur_vals)):
172   
f.write('%s: %s sec \n' % (labels[i], int(np.round(dur_vals[i]))))
173   
174   #%% create gantt chart
175   import pandas as pd
176   
177   plt.close('all')
178   
179   plt.figure(figsize=(12,6))
180   colors = ['k','k','royalblue','r','r','m','m','g','g','g']
181   
182   plt.barh(y=labels, width=dur_vals, left=start_vals,color = colors)#time + 1)
183   plt.title('Gantt Chart of Intervention Timeline', fontsize=15)
184   plt.gca().invert_yaxis()
185   plt.xlabel(r'$time$ - [s]')
186   plt.grid(visible=None, which='major', axis='x')
187   
188   xticks = np.arange(0, 1020+60, 60)
189   plt.xticks(xticks)
190   plt.xticks(rotation=25)
191   plt.yticks(rotation=25)
192   
193   #plt.show()
194   plt.savefig('Gantt_Chart.png',bbox_inches='tight')

labels.append('Chart 10 - SHT 2 (FF 4 waits)')
==PAGE:317==
97   
start_vals.append(chart8_21.time)
98   
dur_vals.append(chart10_21.time-chart8_21.time)
99   
100   milestones['SHT 2 - Water Connection Established'] = [current_time]
101   
102   # Checking that water connection is established (FF 3) before SHT 1 moves to fire compartment!
103   chart9_1 = Chart9.Chart_9(time=0, input_file="main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_1.txt")
104   SHT1_water = chart10_1.time - chart9_1.time # The acc. time where SHT is ready to move to fire compartment if FF3 is 
done
105   
106   chart9_2 = Chart9.Chart_9(time=0, input_file="main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_21.txt")
107   FF3_water = chart10_21.time - chart9_2.time
# The acc. time where FF 3 has established water connection
108   
109   
110   if SHT1_water<FF3_water: # FF 3 is not done before SHT1 is ready to move to fire compartment - SHT 1 needs to wait
111   
SHT1_water = FF3_water + chart9_1.time # The new 'chart10_1.time'
112   
113   
labels.insert(4,'Chart 10 - SHT 1 (w/ wait) \n 1. Attack Line')
114   
start_vals.insert(4,chart8_1.time)
115   
dur_vals.insert(4,SHT1_water-chart8_1.time)
116   
117   
milestones['SHT 1 - Attack Line Established'] = [FF3_water]
118   
milestones['SHT 1 - Fire Control Initiated'] = [SHT1_water]
119   
120   else:
# FF 3 is done before SHT 1 is ready to move to fire compartment - no waiting time
121   
labels.insert(4,'Chart 10 - SHT 1 (w/o wait) \n 1. Attack Line')
122   
start_vals.insert(4,chart8_1.time)
123   
dur_vals.insert(4,chart10_1.time-chart8_1.time)
124   
125   
milestones['SHT 1 - Attack Line Established'] = [SHT1_water]
126   
milestones['SHT 1 - Fire Control Initiated'] = [chart10_1.time]
127   
128   # # BA time for SHT 1
129   # BA_time = 20*60
130   # labels.insert(5,'BA time limit - SHT 1')   
131   # start_vals.insert(5,SHT1_water)           
132   # dur_vals.insert(5,BA_time)    
133   
134   ## CHANGE by V60, Q2 and T2
135   # When SHT 2 have established the water connection, they are to prepare a new water attack by HP-hose:
136   chart10_2 = Chart10.Chart_10(time=current_time, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart10_Exp3_2_case3.txt",
"main_exp3/Chart9_Exp3_1_2.txt"])
137   
138   labels.append('Chart 10 - SHT 2 \n 2. Attack Line')
139   start_vals.append(current_time)
140   dur_vals.append(chart10_2.time-current_time)
141   milestones['SHT 2 - Attack Line Established'] = [chart10_2.time]
142   
143   ## CHANGE by Y1
144   # SHT 2 now perform S&R:
145   chart12 = Chart12.Chart_12(time=chart10_2.time, input_file=["main_exp3/Chart12_Exp3_2.txt"])
==PAGE:318==
146   
147

149   labels.append('Chart 12 - SHT 2')

Appendix E
FBIM Exercises
Firefighter Engineering - Validation of the Fire Brigade Intervention Model in Danish Fire Safety Design
363
==PAGE:371==
 
1
Exercise 1  
Hose Drill 
 
Introduction 
This exercise is part of a series which have been developed to obtain specific statistical data, to 
ensure that necessary provisions are incorporated in building design for fire brigade operational 
tasks, and to ensure fire fighter safety.  The information will be collated for input into a fire 
brigade model for effective brigade activities at time of fire.  While the activities listed may not 
exactly correspond to events on a fire ground, they have been designed for general coverage and 
maximum flexibility of data.  It is acknowledged that on the fire ground, some activities may be 
undertaken simultaneously, and an additional option is provided to complete the activities as a 
single exercise in real time if desired.  The exercises should not be considered as a competitive 
assessment, but normal fire ground speed is required.  No indication of the brigade (except 
brigade type as per AIRS standard) or station is to be included on the activity time sheet. 
 
Drill 
All firefighters to be dressed in full turnout gear.  1 firefighter to establish a feed\inlet from a fire 
hydrant to a pump appliance, 2 firefighters in BA shall set up an attack hose and discharge water.  
The officer-in-charge will record times for each activity.  All work to be carried out at normal fire 
ground speed.  Where possible use 65mm diameter hose.  Only use full hose lengths. 
 
Resources 
• Pump appliance with officer and 3 fire-fighters 
• BA for 2 fire fighters 
• 4 x 30 metre lengths hose 
• Equipment to connect to the hydrant used  (eg. for a below ground hydrant a standpipe will be 
necessary) 
 
Objective 
To establish the time taken for tasks associated with hose operations: 
 
      Water supply to the appliance 
• Connect and charge sufficient 30 m lengths of hose between a fire appliance and the nearest 
hydrant a measured distance from the inlet on the appliance 
 
Delivery from the appliance 
• Withdraw and don BA set, don face mask, test seal and complete BA control procedures 
• Lay and charge not less than two 30 m lengths of delivery hose between a fire appliance and 
branch operator a measured distance from the outlet on the appliance 
==PAGE:372==
 
2
Method 
Position a pump appliance within two hose lengths reach of a fire hydrant and with sufficient 
space to lay and charge to operating pressure (with branch open) a 60 m hose line (see page 3 for 
a diagram of the drill). 
 
Driver engage pump (if cab control), alight, withdraw all necessary equipment to connect to the 
hydrant (eg. adaptors, keys, standpipe, plate lifter, hydrant bar, turn keys, etc.), prepare hydrant 
for connection (eg. ship standpipe, remove cap, flush, fit adaptor, strainer or breaching piece), as 
per normal operational procedure.  Return for the 2 lengths of rolled hose, connect hose and 
charge, return to appliance. 
 
2 Firefighters at signal from officer, alight, don BA and face masks at appliance, lodge BA 
tallies.  For this exercise BA control must be at the appliance, this equipment set up by the 
driver.   Lay hose to designated operation point.  Pump operator to charge lines so branch 
operator can  flow water with appliance delivering at required operating pressure. 
 
Measure and log distance of hydrant from appliance inlet and branch operator position from 
appliance outlet. 
 
 
Notes for the Officer in charge 
It becomes very difficult to write down all the times if the whole drill is carried out as at a fire 
scene.  So much happens at once.  If attempting to work as at a fire scene, times for some 
activities will be missed whilst writing down the times of other activities.  It is therefore 
necessary to break down the process into manageable steps.  As an option, the activities can be 
repeated as a single fire ground exercise so that a total time is determined, however this is IN 
ADDITION to the activity times stipulated on the sheet. 
 
All times are to be recorded in seconds.  A completed sample of exercise 1 provides an example 
of how the times should be recorded.  In the sample, the start time is recorded as zero on three 
occasions because the officer staged the drill in manageable sections, each section starting at 
zero.  The most important time to record is the time taken (3rd column) and if each activity is 
done separately, this is the only column required to be filled out.  Note also the comments.  In the 
sample, this fire crew only had 50 mm diameter delivery hose and insufficient room to lay a 60 m 
hose line. 
 
A fire plug is a SA term for an underground fire hydrant.  These hydrants require a turn-key 
unlike the ball type hydrants used in other parts of Australia such as NSW.  It is most important 
to state what type of hydrant is utilised as there are many different types used in Australia.  If an 
adaptor is used (eg Stortz) which must be screwed onto the hydrant outlet, please record this.  
Similarly if it is your brigades practice to attach a valved breaching piece, or a strainer, then do 
so, but note down on the sheet that you have used this equipment. 
 
It is important that the drill be carried out and should not be cancelled because of unforseen 
difficulties which may be faced in conducting the drill.  The officer should comment on any issue 
which caused a variation to the drill or affected recorded times.  Only the activity time sheet with 
the recorded times need be sent in. 
 
==PAGE:373==

Brigade type (as per AIRS standard): permanent/ composite/ retained/ volunteer/ defence 
==PAGE:375==
 
1
Exercise 2  
Booster Drill 
 
Introduction 
This exercise is part of a series which have been developed to obtain specific statistical data, to 
ensure that necessary provisions are incorporated in building design for fire brigade operational 
tasks, and to ensure fire fighter safety.  The information will be collated for input into a fire 
brigade model for effective brigade activities at time of fire.  While the activities listed may not 
exactly correspond to events on a fire ground, they have been designed for general coverage and 
maximum flexibility of data.  It is acknowledged that on the fire ground, some activities may be 
undertaken simultaneously (such as connecting delivery hose and booster hose), and an 
additional option is provided to complete the activities as a single exercise in real time if desired.  
The exercises should not be considered as a competitive assessment, but normal fire ground 
speed is required.  No indication of the brigade (except brigade type as per AIRS standard) or 
station is to be included on the activity time sheet. 
 
Drill 
This drill is ideally carried out at an industrial complex which has a booster connection and feed 
hydrants from a street main. 
 
All firefighters to be dressed in full turnout gear.  One fire fighter to establish a 60 m single hose 
line feed/inlet from a fire hydrant to a pump appliance, this feed to be taken from a booster 
assembly hydrant or street hydrant.  1 firefighter to connect a 60 m hose line from the appliance 
into the booster and charge the system.  2 firefighters in BA will lay hose from an installed 
hydrant and discharge water at operational pressure.  The officer-in-charge will record times for 
each activity.  All work to be carried out at normal fire ground speed.  Where possible use 65mm 
diameter hose.  Only use full hose lengths. 
 
Resources 
• Pump appliance with officer and 3 fire-fighters 
• BA for 2 firefighters 
• 4 x 30 metre lengths hose 
• Equipment to connect to the hydrant used  (eg. for a below ground hydrant a standpipe will be 
necessary) 
• A hydrant installation which incorporates a booster assembly 
 
Objective 
To establish the time taken for tasks associated with boosting: 
 
      Water supply to the appliance 
• Connect and charge sufficient 30 m lengths of hose between a fire appliance and the nearest 
hydrant a measured distance from the inlet on the appliance 
 
Delivery from the appliance to boosters. 
• Lay and charge sufficient 30 m lengths of delivery hose between a fire appliance and booster 
connections a measured distance from the outlet on the appliance 
• Charge system. 
• Don BA, walk a measured distance and lay, charge and flow attack line. 
==PAGE:376==
 
2
Method 
Position a pump appliance within two hose lengths reach of a fire hydrant and with sufficient 
space to lay and charge hose lines to booster connections and obtain operational pressure at 
discharging hydrant. 
 
Driver only to engage pump (if cab control), alight, withdraw all necessary equipment to connect 
to the hydrant (eg. adaptors, keys, standpipe, plate lifter, hydrant bar, turn keys, etc.), prepare 
hydrant for connection (eg. ship standpipe, remove cap, flush, fit adaptor, strainer or breaching 
piece), as per normal operational procedure.  Return for the 2 lengths of rolled hose, connect hose 
and charge, return to appliance. 
 
1 Firefighter, at signal from officer, alights, lays hose to designated booster point and connect 
into booster inlets.  Pump operator to charge lines and bring system up to operating pressure.  2 
firefighters, at signal from officer, alight, don BA and face masks at appliance, lodge BA tallies. 
For this exercise BA control must be at the appliance, this equipment set up by the driver.  
Carry hose to designated attack hydrant, lay and charge hose, establish a working straight hose 
stream at stable appliance discharge pressure. 
 
Measure and log distance of hydrant from appliance inlet, booster connections from appliance 
outlet, and walked distance from appliance to boosted hydrant. 
 
Notes for the Officer in charge 
It becomes very difficult to write down all the times if the whole drill is carried out as at a fire 
scene.  So much happens at once.  If attempting to work as at a fire scene, times for some 
activities will be missed whilst writing down the times of other activities.  It is therefore 
necessary to break down the process into manageable steps.  As an option, the activities can be 
repeated as a single fire ground exercise so that a total time is determined, however this is IN 
ADDITION to the activity times stipulated on the sheet. 
 
All times are to be recorded in seconds.  A completed sample of exercise 2 provides an example 
of how the times should be recorded.  In the sample, the start time is recorded as zero on those 
occasions that the officer needed to stage the drill in manageable sections.  The most important 
time to record is the time taken (3rd column) and if each activity is done separately, this is the 
only column required to be filled out.  Note also the comments.  In the sample, this fire crew used 
a storz adaptor and the hydrant was an L-type, and the comments also include that the booster 
connections were not labelled correctly. 
 
A fire plug is a SA term for an underground fire hydrant.  These hydrants require a turn-key 
unlike the ball type hydrants used in other parts of Australia such as NSW.  It is most important 
to state what types of hydrant and coupling are utilised as there are many different types used in 
Australia.  If an adaptor is used which must be screwed onto the hydrant outlet, please record 
this.  Similarly if it is your brigades practice to attach a valved breaching piece, or a strainer, then 
do so, but note down on the sheet that you have used this equipment. 
 
It is important that the drill be carried out and should not be cancelled because of unforseen 
difficulties which may be faced in conducting the drill.  The officer should comment on any issue 
which caused a variation to the drill or affected recorded times.  Only the activity time sheet with 
the recorded times need be sent in.

==PAGE:380==
 
1
Exercise 3  
Taking a Hose up Stairs 
 
Introduction 
This exercise is part of a series which have been developed to obtain specific statistical data, to 
ensure that necessary provisions are incorporated in building design for fire brigade operational 
tasks, and to ensure fire fighter safety.  The information will be collated for input into a fire 
brigade model for effective brigade activities at time of fire.  While the activities listed may not 
exactly correspond to events on a fire ground, they have been designed for general coverage and 
maximum flexibility of data.  It is acknowledged that on the fire ground, some activities may be 
undertaken simultaneously (such as connecting delivery hose and donning BA), and an additional 
option is provided to complete the activities as a single exercise in real time if desired.  The 
exercises should not be considered as a competitive assessment, but normal fire ground speed is 
required.  No indication of the brigade (except brigade type as per AIRS standard) or station is to 
be included on the activity time sheet. 
 
Drill 
Initially, 2 firefighters to ascend stairs with high pressure hose utilising water from the appliance 
only. 
 
Task 2 will include establishing a water feed\delivery to the appliance.  All firefighters to be 
dressed in full turnout gear.  One firefighter to establish a feed\inlet from a fire hydrant to a pump 
appliance, two firefighters shall set up an attack hose, hose to be taken up stairs and charged.  
The officer-in-charge will record times for each activity.  All work to be carried out at normal fire 
ground speed.  Where possible use the high pressure hose reel, a 38mm and 65mm diameter hose.  
Only use full hose lengths. 
 
Resources 
• Pump appliance with high pressure hose reel, officer and 3 fire-fighters 
• BA for 2 fire fighters, sufficient lengths of hose 
• Equipment to connect to the hydrant used  (eg. standpipe) 
• Access to stairs (minimum 2 flights of stairs preferred) 
 
Objective 
To establish the task times using high pressure hose, 65 mm & 38 mm diameter attack hose lines: 
 
 
Water source from pumper 
• Position the fire appliance a measured distance from the stair entry. 
• Initially, run the high pressure hose reel utilising the water tank on the pumper only.  Ascend 
stairs and charge hose reel ready for fire attack. 
 
 
Water supply to the appliance 
• Connect and charge sufficient 30 m lengths of hose between a fire appliance and the nearest 
hydrant a measured distance from the inlet on the appliance 
 
 
 
 
Delivery from the appliance 
• Lay sufficient 30 m lengths of 65 mm diameter hose from the fire appliance. 
• Ascend stairs then charge hose ready for fire attack. 
• Repeat using 38 mm diameter hose. 
==PAGE:381==
 
2
Method 
Position an appliance within a measured distance of the stair entry.  2 Firefighters at signal from 
officer, alight, don BA and face masks at appliance, and lodge BA tallies.  Ascend stairs with 
high pressure hose line and charge to operating pressure.  Measure and log distance to stair entry 
and log time to ascend and charge hose. 
 
Position a pump appliance within two hose lengths reach of a fire hydrant and with sufficient 
space to lay and charge to operating pressure a 60 m hose line.  Measure the distances from the 
hydrant to the appliance, and from the appliance to the stair entry. 
 
Driver only to engage pump (if cab control), alight, withdraw all necessary equipment to connect 
to the hydrant (eg. adaptors, keys, standpipe, plate lifter, hydrant bar, turn keys, etc.), prepare 
hydrant for connection (eg. ship standpipe, remove cap, flush, fit adaptor, strainer or breaching 
piece), as per normal operational procedure.  Return for the 2 lengths of rolled hose, connect hose 
and charge, return to appliance. 
 
2 Firefighters at signal from officer, alight, don BA and face masks at appliance, lodge BA 
tallies.  For this exercise BA control must be at the appliance, this equipment set up by the 
driver..   Lay hose and ascend stairs to designated landing.  Pump operator charge lines, water at 
required operating pressure.  Measure and log distance to building entry and number of stairs 
ascended. 
 
Notes for the Officer in charge 
It becomes very difficult to write down all the times if the whole drill is carried out as at a fire 
scene.  So much happens at once.  If attempting to work as at a fire scene, times for some 
activities will be missed whilst writing down the times of other activities.  It is therefore 
necessary to break down the process into manageable steps.  As an option, the activities can be 
repeated as a single fire ground exercise so that a total time is determined, however this is IN 
ADDITION to the activity times stipulated on the sheet. 
 
All times are to be recorded in seconds.  A completed sample of exercise 3 provides an example 
of how the times should be recorded.  In the sample, the start time is recorded as zero on those 
occasions that the officer needed to stage the drill in manageable sections.  The most important 
time to record is the time taken (3rd column) and if each activity is done separately, this is the 
only column required to be filled out.  Note also the comments.  In the sample, the hydrant used 
was a millcock which required a storz adaptor. 
 
A fire plug is a SA term for an underground fire hydrant.  These hydrants require a turn-key 
unlike the ball type hydrants used in other parts of Australia such as NSW.  It is most important 
to state the type of hydrant and coupling utilised as there are many different types used in 
Australia.  If an adaptor is used which must be screwed onto the hydrant outlet, please record 
this.  Similarly if it is your brigades practice to attach a valved breaching piece, or a strainer, then 
do so, but note down on the sheet that you have used this equipment. 
 
It is important that the drill be carried out and should not be cancelled because of unforseen 
difficulties which may be faced in conducting the drill.  The officer should comment on any issue 
which caused a variation to the drill or affected recorded times.  Only the activity time sheet with 
the recorded times need be sent in.

Exercise 4 
Personnel movement 
 
Introduction 
This exercise is part of a series which have been developed to obtain specific statistical data, 
to ensure that necessary provisions are incorporated in building design for fire brigade 
operational tasks, and to ensure fire fighter safety.  The information will be collated for 
input into a fire brigade model for effective brigade activities at time of fire.  While the 
activities listed may not exactly correspond to events on a fire ground, they have been 
designed for general coverage and maximum flexibility of data.  The exercises should not be 
considered as a competitive assessment, but normal fire ground speed is required.  No 
indication of the brigade (except brigade type as per AIRS standard) or station is to be 
included on the activity time sheet. 
 
Drill 
2 Firefighters to be dressed in full turnout gear, walk a measured distance (approximately 
50m) dressed in BA, then ascend a number of stair flights (more than 3 is preferable).  
Conduct task as appropriate (refer table), then descend stairs.  Crew members to take 
appropriate rest times as necessary. 
All activities to be conducted simulating fire ground conditions. 
 
Resources 
• Pump appliance with crew 
• High rise pack or similar (minimum 1 length 38 mm diameter hose, branch and adaptors) 
 
Objective 
To establish horizontal and vertical walking times, over measured distances, in BA and 
carrying equipment.  Drill should be conducted in a clear (no smoke) environment. 
 
Method 
Dismount appliance, remove and don BA and collect high rise pack or similar. 
Conduct BA procedures and safety checks at forward control point. 
Walk measured horizontal distance to building entry point. 
Ascend measured stairs at normal walking speed 
Connect and deploy hose line (dry) and prepare for use 
 
Notes for the Officer in charge 
It becomes very difficult to write down all the times if the whole drill is carried out as at a 
fire scene.  So much happens at once.  If attempting to work as at a fire scene, times for some 
activities will be missed whilst writing down the times of other activities.  It is therefore 
necessary to break down the process into manageable steps.  As an option, the activities can 
be repeated as a single fire ground exercise so that a total time is determined, however this is 
IN ADDITION to the activity times stipulated on the sheet. 
 
All times are to be recorded in seconds.  A completed sample of exercise 4 shows that if each 
activity is done separately, only column 3 is required to be filled out.  Note also the 
comments.  In the sample, this fire crew used a high rise pack with the equipment listed. Only 
the activity time sheet with the recorded times need be sent in.
